Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When such pain reaches the head (chief), it spreads out as an illness there and dislocates are cleansed with pure medicines, all other treatments have been done according to what I've mentioned in dividing diseases; none of this benefits.

Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The treatments of bloodletting if you begin with an amount and remove the bark and peel as II (two) pieces, then make a hole in it such that you can apply the quantity to stop the pain.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is put back on if the ligament and strain are done well, leave for this much time. (12 hours)

Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After placing the screw of the shoulder hinge above their chest skinny person, and press your hand up on the screw of the shoulder hinge;
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After pouring between the two heated circles of the cauterized area made hot by the fire poker and leaving it for an hour, letting the patients endure the heat and scalding from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For fear also arises likewise with fire;  
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	And when the bites are not passed on, take your hand with the instrument and raise the shoulder screw gently, allowing it to stay in place for three years, until the black residue from the bite is healed.
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	And leave them three years while they pass through infancy.
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the rear support aid after the treatment of ointments until he is healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, let it increase according to what you have done in dealing with hip inflammation.
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And that is the way of applying heat, and I have written or treated it as a remedy for correction of medicines.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Use quicklime and fresh chalk together, grind them all up, then place them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	Or let there be a small hole so that the point of an arrow can enter it.
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and place there another piece well-forged upon it, and put sulphur and charcoal on top of them, so much that you will have two above the powders with which to lightly strike.
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and leave it so long until the smoke and sparks fly out from there, then take all of it away, and pour it into charcoal and sulphur as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And when there is moaning from the wounds of medicines and other parts requiring cupping or similar treatments, it means they are in pain seeking relief through these methods.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it performs as we do when caustically treating the hip joint here in this way—cauterizing well with charcoal and sulphur like honey and soap used together to soothe—these combined actions form a cohesive therapeutic effort.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galiens tells us about a treatment for the pain of the hip and sciatic nerve, which involved exercise (loe mout), stating that no other remedy was attempted before this one, after which he became sound once more when they performed this cure, even bathing in it as instructed.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	Then spread it thinly that you might begin the poultice of fresh and dry litargy (a medicinal salve or ointment), crush it with some fat drops, apply it to the hip joint and thigh, where the pain holds sway, and leave it there.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And let it stay for three hours as long as none of his patients feel any more discomfort from the arthritis or joint pain after applying this remedy according to their needs.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then have him enter the bath until his flesh is sufficiently warm, and let him into bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be cleansed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And none should use such hot treatments unless after the evacuation of blood from wounds.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Diogenes Caius says that when the sciatic nerve is cauterized with goat hairs, if it helps.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and should be done in moderation manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wax and honey ointment, and place it on the crease between the thumb of your foot and the other called phalanges.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After taking dry hides and putting them on fire until they are chars, then placing them in the wool for as long as they remain tan.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and continue to do so hereafter as well, and keep doing it until you think that the pain will be gone down to this joint.
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	And this method of fire cupping is called "cupping with sheep bladder.

et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	And make such cauterizations in accordance with what is called "points".

de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the joints
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is fat that accumulates under the skin of papers above them, and this occurs more in children than adults, causing great discomfort to their eyes, making it impossible for them to look at the sunlight in the mornings as tears start streaming down.

de la char sor le neis	From flesh to bone
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Never do they seem to come out of their joints variously, from which it appears that some are like scorpions at the base of bone.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	And if he has such skin or flesh of fire-colored hue, and the bony part also colored by flame.

adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Advise you to tie up the large flax thread with your hands, and leave enough space between each one of us.

li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of apothecaries' stones (interpreted as "the texts

When abscesses arise near joinings and are left there while they remain redolent (implying heat or feverish), potentially if the ligaments and nerves of that joining become spoiled thus causing contraction in the limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or when cauterization occurs at the main part of the limb and if puncturing is delayed until it has died out, harm will befall upon that primary member. et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	After the application of moisture is gone, if it becomes greasy and he does so with knives taking out pieces selectively from various parts along its path where you wear clothes to keep clean.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If you cannot remove it safely, do so in pieces; if nothing is left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	And when there's nothing left to clean up, it comes back to us many times over.

Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is inside belly or breast, ensure that you remove it with a cloth held in your hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and when the abdomen or breast contains wetness, continue until those excesses are removed.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if other members are out of joint and it seeks restraint, bind the limb that is protruding from pain with cloth held in hand. Remove along its edges at the mouth of inflammation.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the healer's care and I thought for long times without being able to stop her wound bleeding out continuously.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed it under strong magnetism, and from there came an osteon, and after several days another one appeared.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I vomited upwardly, for my belly had no bone within it.

et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	And this is the common method for dressings, and you must use either needles or more of them depending on the size of the wound's opening. This detailed guidance speaks to traditional approaches used by medieval healers, incorporating materials like needles and threads into their treatment regimens for serious injuries such as large or deep cuts. des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that grow between hide and wood.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is prevalent in our land as the "cattle sickness," for it occurs frequently through fleas and concerns itself with tiny worms that emerge between hide and wood. It ascends and descends throughout the body from joint to joint, feeling quite severe along each limb until it either destroys leather or continues its movement;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is infested with various fluids, just like worms and roundworms and Ascaris enter the body.

de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from windy discomfort or pain caused by drafts, which often aggravates the patient's
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is said to be spread in our land "virikir," and it's pain that comes into any member, moving from one limb to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I showed you this one here.

et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And then again, I see it mount up here as quickly as a worm in the shoulder, faster than anything else, just like quick silver when cutting through another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departs from the joint that was dislocated and settles in the shoulder blade, then quickly spreads throughout the entire arm until it reaches the other elbow.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told that she twisted into a spiral within her joint, just as I saw it.

Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I had wanted to move the pain from joint to joint but never did until seeing her.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because she had a tight joint and discovered women with such conditions seem bound by this windless constraint.

des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their appearances and by their joints or where they prick.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of them is that some have large points, and others small, with hairs, and soldered together.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those with two joints, or those who have tongues, and of those that are broken.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And those who wince in any part of their body according to these two methods.
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	In their primary member (hair), if like a brain, liver, gallbladder, portal vein, kidney, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When they cease in any of these members, and the sign of death appears to you as I tell you hereafter.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you must extract this arrow, for the bite comes after more things are arranged in your disposition.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if this bad sign does not appear to you at all, and the arrow is yet untouched by lance or treatment; then as your trail proceeds, so shall be treated for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces and penetrates bone is that which causes scotomia (blindness) above the skull, turning it sideways, reddening eyes internally, inflammation with a dragging tongue movement, spasm affecting understanding, vomiting from collection [likely referring to gallstones], etc.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And perhaps without nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and possibly affecting speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from the wet wound looking like scales, and so it bleeds as if cut by iron;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and signs appear on you which heal when treated with the remedy, and draw out the arrowhead if it is not entangled;
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign when the arrowhead bends or breaks is that it presses against the left breastbone and feels as if it were a hard object not void of substance. In plain English: When an arrow lodges in your body (breastbone), you'll feel pressure on the side where the injury occurred, similar to feeling something solid but empty inside;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow becomes mute in its movement like bone fragments and black blood flows out with cold sweat, causing chills and a faint pulse followed by loss of consciousness;
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	so they then doubt whether their limb will move again.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that is not accompanied by blood from the wound causes swelling in the throat, and their lips turn blueish-purple, and they gasp for air loudly and ask about death.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if arrows sink under their covering here, they are near the small bones.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and cause great pain and suspicion;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and they move their shoulder joints.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow or wound causes vomiting from adventure—if there is no internal damage to meat due to injury through it.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces or enters and does not find hope in healing nor extraction of the arrow from the intestines.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And when the arrow pierces into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes to spill forth, and the patients feel great pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	and if it is deadly wounds.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if like the face and neck and shoulder and elbow and scapula and spine of the back and thigh and head parts, and seemingly appearing members are according to various arrangements safe.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the saw is in the nerve or artery and not injured, as I tell you so that you might do it yourself.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened at his home with an arrow or litter falling on its root.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and then applied pressure to the ear's fat, resulting in healing.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And in one instance he tried an arrow that had fallen into the ear's fat layer and was repositioned. The pointed end of the iron-tipped bowstring protruded from his ears at all times as if to emphasize their hearing ability, especially since it seemed particularly heavy or substantial like a Turkish bowstring might be made from strong material suitable for drawing attention through its size alone:

et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And then after having passed for so many years without changing his arrangement;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I tied it up under the arrow, and I grasped it firmly, and extracted it without any injury occurring to me.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you find yourself at home where an arrow fell or caused a wound that was sealed there;   
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	Let him keep his arrow at hand, and not change his natural disposition; nor find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And look to another man who was hit by an arrow and had his wound sutured up.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	And continue in this way, enduring great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And he treated an arrow from the prince's house that lay within him, which was held by pressure on the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and was the arrow all reset.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I called for her to come after this, which took three years.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound was narrowed or constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I asked her at every subtle hint, and she did not feel it then either.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt the pressure and pain in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was the point of the arrow I placed on his backward chewing organ, so that their teeth would not burst. (Note: The translation reflects an understanding that "emplaustre atratifet digestiv" likely refers to a part of the gastrointestistic system or stomach in contemporary language.)
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw her teeth from the arrow appeared. (The text suggests that seeing something emerged related to an arrow, which might imply blood clots or bone
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the cautery on my hands for a whole year, and healed his wound with it, and kept them stretched so long as he felt the arrow in his neck that day.
et il le me dist.	And he gave it to me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied medicinal quicklime to the wound for weeks until it healed completely and tried applying it there, feeling where the arrowhead protruded in its place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I removed it from the opening of the wound with quicklime medicinal as long as the arrowhead was visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And passed it well within three months and then seized the saws with both hands on my side, cutting into them to remove what was left of it. I couldn't extricate any further by hand alone now.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I never ceased to refine and tighten the tools in my hands until I take it each day with well-made nails, according as that form will come at the end of this chapter, so long as I treat it, and heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the nasal septum cannot restore itself.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will repair it myself and thereby heal the wound completely; thus I cured the patient entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	You mentioned the quality of arrow extractions as if you could grasp everything that I do not say because books cannot comprehend all. (Note: This sentence is a bit more complex and abstract in meaning, but it attempts to translate the content.)
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the masters of this craft bestow nine times over and use fresh instruments for extracting things that come into their skill in handling them.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I declare they sprout from limbs or where, according to two methods.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the bone (by piercing it) or otherwise;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And when it jumps through or into their body cavity, that is a seed entering the fleshly core, and will not happen again now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump anymore, as long as the flesh is putrefying and agony lingers for her departure.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is lodged in the bone and cannot leave, provided she does not remove herself hereafter each day for growth.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it jumps again, and if not, through any subtle entrance until the flesh is expanded therein; then she extracts (it).
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the seed is lodged in the bone at the head of the joint and wanders just to one side of the brain cavity, none of the troubles I have mentioned will apply (to this situation).
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	Do not remove it but leave it until it is even after any number of seasons, for its screw comes just as in the case; that is, if you pull out a nail, then there will be blood loss similar to drawing teeth.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed just by bone alone and does not come out through his shirt, and causes patients to fear any injury each day until it draws blood from an internal wound.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is so moist that it cannot issue forth forcefully, then I administer torches accordingly as I have instructed you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the joint until it is healed and healthy again.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if you cannot see its socket put back into place in the joint, it is as though all of your efforts are futile. If fear has tightened around everything for them to grasp onto, nothing they attempt will succeed.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it too sensitive with no suitable instruments at hand.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot reach the depth of the wound or straighten out the socket and it has no bone nor sinew to heal with as long as the injury remains great.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And remove the arrow if you use it, and if there are ears in the arrow that hold on tightly to what is fixed at its two parts for movement when used by you, take out or bend those ears of the arrow as much as you can.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And subtly without breaking the arrowhead, pull it out more tightly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove once, keep pulling until the bones are broken, because extraction is laborious then.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding makes you contrary, bring forth what we have said about healing in this chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	And subject it to the incision of nerve and vein, applying as much strength or delicacy you choose in removing the arrowhead without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and have the patient follow the form they were in when the arrow hit them, for it is the greatest aid that one can provide and if you cannot do so, then according to what signs show on you must place them.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or it has nothing of its own attached to it, or the skin is swollen in this spot where one can see or feel apart.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	So size up now until the pincers can grasp it, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it has sprung out already.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly while it enters into the bone and then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot remove it, then let her continue to hold on until she forces it out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if it was from an arrowhead, then its entire form is.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if it was pierced and you see to administer bandaging, provided that the arrowhead of your instrument enters into the hair of the tool.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And then it is pushed outwardly, and its saw-like instrument enters in herein, for the purpose of extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, you must cover all of it or wherever the poison enters, as long as you can do so, then treat the wound accordingly.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow pierces or lodges in the belly or bladder and it is imminent, you must cover over there as well, covering each one of them.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	Do not cover the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and that is how you master this.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and until she (the patient) becomes healthy again.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pincers used for treating arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and herein lies their shape.
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And they are composed of such methods/techniques. (Note: The translation attempts to capture the original meaning
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Great sizes and small ones, according to the quantity of the arrowheads required. (Here 'according' is used instead of 'depending on', as it fits more naturally in this context; additionally, I have translated 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead's point is like that of a bird'dict pen; to place at the tip of the arrowhead similarly as it. (Note: The translation maintains parallel structure by comparing "the form" in both instances, and attempts to convey similarity between the two objects.)
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the pincers for holding and for seizing if this is so stated.
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common arrows
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	The number of arrows from which one recovers is XXXI, referring to it as having or head XVII. It means that there are thirty-one such items with seventeen being the key component mentioned hereinforth.
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	The ones after the ears, which are called "dry grass";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries appearing from the second chambers;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins in the second lumbar discs, which are called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	And the vein where it enters at the face;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein located in the neck.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two grooves which are or course through it (possibly referring to nerve pathways around a joint);
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins located underneath the lips, and these are called "auger" (likely referring to blood vessels);
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins in the tongue;
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The typical number of vessels commonly found is five per arm (possibly referring to arteries, as this context seems medical);
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the carotid (possibly referring to its role in supplying blood to the brain), located on the left side of the neck and called "head vein" by laypeople. This line also suggests an informal naming convention used for identification among non-medical people, which could be less precise or medically accurate;
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and its removal is fastened ("faste"), composed of the cranial and pelvic parts, and called by people "body vein".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is located on the lower abdominal side ("costeit"), and called by people "body vein" ("voinne dou ventre"), situated above (or in line with) the bladder, which clearly presents itself through the belly-button hole.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And it is the vein located between the little finger and ring finger, and if two of them.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg or thigh are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	The one on either side of the curve of the left shoulder blade and the second which is at the knee joint of the right leg.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the vein that has been drawn out, it's in the knee of the other leg.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other limb are three such veins as well.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The veins after the ears aid ancient draining methods and in migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the quality of such veins, if I tell you so and it's that you treat with utmost care to your main physician (or doctor), and rub or apply these veins with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then gently press the patient's neck using a device (a kind of brace or similar apparatus), until the two veins appear behind their ears in second position dependent on the head's main physician.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Seek out thy two doctors for thee, and where thou feelest pain upon thine shoulders, if sovereign of it.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Take up the needle and use it through thy vein just above bone, then lift your hand towards the vein's head, pressing firmly on the skin and blood vessel well in twofold. Continue until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then bind tightly until she is healthy again.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already mentioned the incision and the caustic in our first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The two veins in the Second Temple that are old and dampened now must be migrated away from it (likely referring to removing them), along with accustomed eyesight, dry skin on the lips, and swolthy points of sores at the corners of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And as for the quality of a healthy body if it is such that I have spoken about:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and he must straighten his neck until both shoulders are appearing openly. (This translation suggests an action related to physically opening up or uncovering the areas around one's shoulder blades.)
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and he feels his lips together and then closes them tightly. (This line is about touching or feeling the inside of the mouth before constricting it.)
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then gently stroke the vein at your top toe joint with one hand and insert a needle above it. Open the lancet near that spot, then touch upwards on the vein if you have done so in other venous points, and make an incision according to necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then lift your patient's leg, place it on the vein for one hour, then put a linen or cloth over.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And shape them into form and leave until they are sound;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	We have spoken about their cauterization and extraction methods or the beginning of a book on these topics;
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The soundness of the vein at the forehead is worth just as much as head-related ancient diseases' ill health and migraines, and with red eyes. (Note: The original text seems to be mixing concepts related to both venous conditions in the face/forehead area ("cephalic") and common ailments of olden times; however, modern medical translation requires careful interpretation as these might not correspond exactly to contemporary understanding.)
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and so long as his voice appears when he bends over.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "dolor," which has this shape herein described. (Note: The term 'fosseur' is not standard English and appears to be medieval or historical terminology that may require further context for accurate translation.)
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point under the vein, holding it firmly with your hand or another object, and let blood flow out according to the amount you see. Then apply pressure to the patient's chest and bind their vein until it is clean and bloodless; (Note: 'flaime wide' could be interpreted as a broad or extensive bandaging, possibly indicating that no gauze was used.)

et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And the sound of health should be straightened; for the bone is pressed tightly and by chance breaks his limb when it is subtle.

Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The vein in the neck if it's valued at feverishness, and from headaches caused by exposure to cold or sickness like a migraine that comes into existence when old.

Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and involves treatment for a break or dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	See here, friendless man, that the fool does not see this chapter again and has never read any of its ancient books or letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason is extracted the knowledge from our land because I found none good.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing except that through the study of ancient books and experiments, as well as my life's custom.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained within it and summarized the shapes of limbs that are brought herein as if they were done so throughout these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Thus we must say the contents of this book and comprehend these chapters with our understanding; so that those who have tried to understand it will learn its noble science from each other.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	When any breakage or dislocation occurs at no joint without exception, you must attend to the patient's wound as much on one side and another, if like fortune of flesh or bone.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	When they hold it too cold or too hot;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	And to extinguish cold fever is known as ice jwts (frozen boots and hare fur), and no meat that fills the veins with blood should be drunk or consumed excessively, nor greasy char horses, until there is doubt of a hot abscess swelling in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If it returns to them for earlier treatment with medicine before their first visit or consultation date;  
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the bones begin to heal, they may need to administer thickened or cooked meats that cause heavy burping, along with beer and wine (and other similar items), such as fried pies, offal, fresh fish, hard liquor, etc.  
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	When there is moisture, they move more quickly and sooner upon breaking down.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And you should know that bones of old and brittle cannot be well maintained or mended according to their natural state, nor can they do so if they are too tender, just as with the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no remedy for it, reset the bone in its position as if before. Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And see how fractures are various through many methods.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	And note that the fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the leg, and I shall explain all methods for this in our chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that occur by falling onto the head, and others resulting from sharp objects, just as one would chip a nib of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And in cases where there is both injury and breakage, with even the smallest crack involved.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each method has its tool and instrument for restoration, according to what comes into his mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the breakage of bone by twisting it and breaking well apart for pressing with one's hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when it does not have twisting or its joints hurt him greatly, he has no breakage.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may have twistiness, or a crack, or a small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it's not enough to move with your hands alone, but by means of the remedies that come next herein described, and then gently restrain now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when the fracture that is coming downhill occurs and they are two joints dislocated, you must bring them back into alignment sockets can bear weight.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And when chalk is applied to it, if he leaves no day until the application becomes soothed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then he places it immobile in such movement that you may lift lightly and carefully, making sure the restoration of his limb is lighter than its previous state with fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then hold on tightly, as he shall afterwards require it to do so.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if it is in the bones shattered into pieces, whether by hand or instrument (like hands themselves for small limbs), or with two instruments and your own hand, these are to be addressed: fingers/limbs broken off, either one at a time using tools like tweezers (`II pars`), directly if they involve smaller members of the body, jointed structures such as arms flexors (hands) or tendons (cordes), or with two instruments and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the limb according to its natural shape so that when parts of the member break and fear sets in, you can apply all additions as needed without causing injury or pain through your efforts.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And align well the two ends of the bones according to their best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And make sure it feels comfortable in your hand if you think it's not quite right already.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If the dressing is done well and not too tightly squeezed or stretched like they often do in their attempts with cautery applied directly to bone heating and contracting movements of the limb. Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is at rest, well instruct the patient not to move it either while awake or asleep, nor in turning, nor by any other means.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	Ensure that the limbs are so secure they do not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	When there is no pain, it's certainly better than before, and he will aim for a position where he does not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And keep him so that his posture is straightened out, lest twisting occurs when he restores himself;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and according to what I tell you, its quality of being broken is thus determined.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Accordingly, the fracture in their small and large sizes and shapes can be identified.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For it has little members like bones and arrows of similar kinds:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	Cover them with fine woolen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And those that are thick like legs and arms.
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And if they require a thick and sturdy bandage, because these bands encircle the entire large limb, compressing all parts evenly, provided there is no residual swelling.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then apply tight bandages, three turns or four according to the limb, and hold your hand firmly around the entire bandage, then go up above the fracture and tighten less so that the fragment slightly moves away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And loosen the bandage a little and again, so long as you preserve some part of healthy flesh above it. Then take another bandage and tighten downward on the injured limb once more.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part of the fracture and gently apply pressure, not too tight nor too hastily, as we have said in the first attempt above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then bind with strips of linen or cloth until it is entirely stable, then tie above using the bandage you have prepared; and place your pins well underneath if there's an abscess or swelling present.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess present, apply something that soothes the inflammation and alleviates discomfort without causing additional issues for as long.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then tighten your bandages accordingly and use strips of cloth that have been washed cleanly or wooden splints shaped into the required form; made from these materials according to this description.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But he must ensure that the bone set used for fractures is larger and wider than others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long or suitable according to the size of the limb.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then is stretched out and spun with flax thread just like in the first application to the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	and becomes narrower as needed.

Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method to immobilize broken bones involves resetting the position of the fragments directly, potentially using splints or similar techniques for stabilization during healing.

Take dried leaves of fig and olive tree branches, grind them together thoroughly, then make an immobilization device with the powdered mix for setting a broken bone in place. Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of immobilization more than the first, when abscess wound is being restored to limb.

et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And grind them finely, and mix with salted water or sweet wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	And in his book he says that nothing but wax and oil is used to mend a broken limb until it rests; none else more tenderly or harder than necessary for the treatment, as stated therein.

Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many breaking methods exist, and they take different forms, with their origins determined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	because there are breaks caused by the striking of a spear or anything that can shatter bone as does an axe or gunpowder.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And for this type of breakage, we call it "hachuring.

et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and it is for these great or small breaks in place.

et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	If the wound made by a sword cut, or fall, or something similar, and brings bone fragments inside, and is as sharp as when blacksmiths work on hot irons.
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the thighbone therein lies.

de la brisure de l’espaule	From the break of the shoulder:
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Whenever the shoulder breaks or widens its joints without moving, and only by contact.

et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and he must have six positions or more for his arms.

et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	And is more stretched than elsewhere during fracturing, and all year round less in exposing it, as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	And let their clothes not be hard or rough when subjected to cautery and moisture.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and make the thread used for tying it not too thick nor too thin as we have said before.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward their limb and ligament afterwards, with no delay or postponement.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any accident occurs to the limb, as when itching comes upon a limb, they must immerse the limb in hot water until that which is itching subsides.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	Let there be no constraint for rest on the affected member.

Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint. Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things come to the patient within XX days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or if none of these things come to the patient within XX days. de la brisure de la main	of the dislocation (or injury) to the hand/arm
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	When at the back of our hand there are a few fractures left and only bends many times over.

de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken bone

et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	Put their eyes to bear the pain on the anchorite's back, then press with the other hand down towards their groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is out of place, they must not extend downward or lift upwards towards heaven as we have described for leg lifting in positions two.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And place it on its face, and stretch out as we have said before, pressing upon the joint to the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and will be straightened when the patient extends their legs, becoming even and level.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the shoulder pins (potentially referring to a joint or arm support), and place/set up an emplastrum (a dressing) along with strapping for binding if so that the hinge does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rests three or four days then it is removed and placed again with an emplastrum on top. (This sentence suggests a healing regimen where the treatment—possibly some form of dressing or support—is changed after a certain period.)
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if they are straightened and the strain is present as before, leave it for three more days. (Here a similar healing time frame to what was mentioned previously applies.)
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Then reset it, and let your arm go lightly so long as the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the joint's dislocation in terms of ligaments (assuming 'genoil
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The displacement is treated according to three methods. (Note that "III" likely refers to a Roman numeral system used for numbering, translating
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	which involves above and below, as well as behind;  
et ne desalue point devant.	and does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And if you order the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and it does not hold there, then they are dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And for the restoration of all this when you make the patient sit with their leg extended if they can, and place your back under their face, and put their pelvis on your knees.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	Then take your thigh between your palms, then bend the two sides of the knee formed by it.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	And other ministers extend his foot until the thigh returns to its place and it indicates that he is walking properly on his kneecap.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	And apply the plaster above it and firmly secure his leg at the kneecap for three to four years or two full years, then remove. (Note: The translation is based on the given text structure but understanding of medieval medical terms might require further context.)
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And do not work out patients until their limbs are comfortable. (Note: The translation attempts to maintain the original meaning while converting old French terms into modern English.)
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place again, as we have mentioned in the treatment of hip joints, until it regains health. (Note: This translation continues with an effort to convey directives from medieval medical practices into contemporary English.)
de la dislocation dou talon	Of a dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never rubbed dry completely, and from within they draw forth moisture, inwards and outwards.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And if it is observed that the ankle is swollen, try at the part where it has been displaced.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And if there are signs that the ankle is swollen, then it should be supported firmly with its hands when moved gently.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And once it is displaced completely, they must make the patient sit up straight and use their leg to apply pressure just above the ankle joint.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then pull tightly with your right hand and then the left twice, lift it upwards firmly, and hold steadily at this high position.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	And do this two times as we have said, squeezing and pulling the ankle joint.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	When she returns, so be it.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	But if the operation occurs again, for it comes back;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	If it cannot return to its place so quickly, let the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly press down in between their ribs, holding a cloth tightly around them so they do not bleed.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then you infect the chest with fleas, and other ministers stretch out their hands or to his body where they touch him on the breastplate of iron.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extends servants evenly, and the instrument lies between the joints of the patient to hold them in place while they are being treated.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then places the jewel on the displaced joint with care, and other ministers bind the healthy leg together; thereupon the dislocation returns quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it reaches that point, they place the plaster and secure them in position; as for the straps, tie them to the leg where they join with the ankle behind, ensuring that none are too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leaves it for two or three days and adjusts the straps if necessary.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	After that period—two to four hours respectively—and definitely brings up their patient for two more days. et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	If he proceeds further ahead, it is not safe for him to continue onwards.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you come upon stones in the way, it is necessary that you soothe him as we have advised elsewhere, until he regains health.
des dois	The necessary ones (or) those
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When these are dislocated, if they wish to extend themselves as though working, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if they are in any dislocation of the back or hip (if it is necessary to make them sit on their loin bone or tabletop straight), and place your pillow under these joints while pressing firmly until they return.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is stationary and does not open (does not move), place the foot of your pillow on their feet at two points ("II" meaning "two"), then stretch them firmly for three days, then release.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it rest until healthy again. (End of translation)
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with dislocation, one must seek to restore it, often until the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not careful in the treatment and do not have experience with it, nor piety or mercy if used for a short time only, and pity is lacking—then be humble, never bold. (Note: This translation attempts to preserve as much of the original meaning while conveying grammatical correctness.)
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And begin with calming measures at first touch, and let the patient hold in their hand a divine symbol if there is no hope for health. (Note: Here again I've tried to maintain fidelity to Old French structures while translating into modern English.)
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope and now reposition the limb in place, so that your incision heals. (This line suggests immediate action upon regaining patient optimism.)
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in place, if you administer cooling compresses applied internally and treat the wound as it requires, using dehydrating ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And with the dislocation there is fragmentation, if bones and small pieces are broken off as we have noted in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	Hold back from entering a state of fear, as I have instructed you, for this is your movement according to your Creator, and by the strength of your armor and body.
